---
title: "Bibliography"
template: page
---

<p id="abad2018">
Abad, Zahra Shakeri Hossein, Oliver Karras, Kurt Schneider, Ken Barker,
and Mike Bauer. 2018. “Task Interruption in Software Development
Projects: What Makes Some Interruptions More Disruptive Than
Others?” <em>arXiv</em>, ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/ARXIV.1805.05508">10.48550/ARXIV.1805.05508</a>.
 <em>Mixed-methods study (longitudinal task analysis of 17 devs + 132-dev survey); contextual factors (interruption type, time of day, task type) predict task-switching disruptiveness more than task-specific factors; self-interruptions more disruptive than external ones, contrary to developer belief.</em></p>
<p id="abate2020">
Abate, Pietro, Roberto Di Cosmo, Georgios Gousios, and Stefano
Zacchiroli. 2020. “Dependency Solving Is Still Hard, but We Are
Getting Better at It.” <em>2020 IEEE 27th Conference on Software
Analysis, Evolution and Reengineering (SANER)</em>, ahead of print,
February. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/saner48275.2020.9054837">10.1109/saner48275.2020.9054837</a>.
 <em>Reviews dependency solving as NP-complete problem; surveys state-of-the-art package managers; SAT-based solving gaining traction but outsourcing to reusable solver components has not; identifies emerging challenges.</em></p>
<p id="abdalkareem2021">
Abdalkareem, Rabe, Suhaib Mujahid, Emad Shihab, and Juergen Rilling.
2021. “Which Commits Can Be CI Skipped?” <em>IEEE
Transactions on Software Engineering</em> 47 (March). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2019.2897300">10.1109/tse.2019.2897300</a>.
 <em>Rule-based technique to auto-identify CI-skippable commits; trained/validated on 58 Java projects; AUC 0.56-0.98, average 18% CI reduction; survey of 40 devs confirms demand; prototype tool CI-Skipper released.</em></p>
<p id="abdalkareem2017">
Abdalkareem, Rabe, Olivier Nourry, Sultan Wehaibi, Suhaib Mujahid, and
Emad Shihab. 2017. “Why Do Developers Use Trivial Packages? An
Empirical Case Study on NPM.” <em>Proc. European
Software Engineering Conference/International Symposium on the
Foundations of Software Engineering (ESEC/FSE)</em>,
August. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3106237.3106267">10.1145/3106237.3106267</a>.
 <em>Empirical study of trivial packages in npm; questions whether extreme code reuse via minimal packages is safe or beneficial following high-profile breakage incidents.</em></p>
<p id="abdelsalam2025">
Abdelsalam, Youssef, Norman Peitek, Anna-Maria Maurer, Mariya Toneva,
and Sven Apel. 2025. <em>How Do Humans and LLMs Process Confusing
Code?</em> <a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2508.18547">https://arxiv.org/abs/2508.18547</a>.
 <em>Empirical study comparing LLM perplexity to human neurophysiological (EEG) responses on clean vs. confusing code; LLM perplexity spikes correlate in location and amplitude with human confusion signals; proposes LLM-based tool to identify confusing code regions.</em></p>
<p id="acciai2023">
Acciai, Claudia, Jesper W. Schneider, and Mathias W. Nielsen. 2023.
“Estimating Social Bias in Data Sharing Behaviours: An Open
Science Experiment.” <em>Scientific Data</em> 10 (April). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/s41597-023-02129-8">10.1038/s41597-023-02129-8</a>.
 <em>Preregistered randomized audit experiment (N=1634) on data-sharing bias; 54% response rate, 14% sharing rate; no confirmed gender/status bias but Chinese-named requestors got systematically lower responses; male Chinese requestors faced lowest willingness, attributed to stereotypic trustworthiness beliefs.</em></p>
<p id="acher2026">
Acher, Mathieu, and Jean-Marc Jézéquel. 2026. <em>Do Programming
Languages Still Matter to Your AI Coding Agent Teammate? Evidence at
Scale from Chess Engines</em>. <a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13763">https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13763</a>.
 <em>Claude Code and Codex produced working chess engines in all 17 tested languages including esoteric ones, but strong Elo is only achievable in mainstream compiled languages and cost grows sharply for exotic targets.</em></p>
<p id="adams2021">
Adams, Sophie, Sheree Bekker, Yanan Fan, et al. 2021. “Gender Bias
in Student Evaluations of Teaching: ’Punish[ing] Those Who Fail to Do
Their Gender Right’.” <em>Higher Education</em> 83 (March). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s10734-021-00704-9">10.1007/s10734-021-00704-9</a>.
 <em>Qualitative study at an Australian university finds student evaluations of teaching measure conformity with gendered expectations rather than teaching quality, with particularly negative effects for women.</em></p>
<p id="agarwal2026">
Agarwal, Shyam, Hao He, and Bogdan Vasilescu. 2026. <em>AI IDEs or
Autonomous Agents? Measuring the Impact of Coding Agents on Software
Development</em>. <a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.13597">https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.13597</a>.
 <em>Longitudinal causal study (staggered diff-in-diff) of coding agent adoption in OSS repos; velocity gains large but front-loaded and only when agents are the first AI tool; quality risks (18% more warnings, 39% higher complexity) persist regardless; highlights need for quality safeguards and selective deployment.</em></p>
<p id="aghajani2019">
Aghajani, Emad, Csaba Nagy, Olga Lucero Vega-Marquez, et al. 2019.
“Software Documentation Issues Unveiled.” <em>Proc.
International Conference on Software Engineering
(ICSE)</em>, May. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/icse.2019.00122">10.1109/icse.2019.00122</a>.
 <em>Large-scale empirical study mining 878 documentation artifacts from mailing lists, Stack Overflow, issue trackers, PRs; produces taxonomy of documentation issues; provides actionable recommendations for researchers and practitioners.</em></p>
<p id="ahadi2016">
Ahadi, Alireza, Julia Prior, Vahid Behbood, and Raymond Lister. 2016.
“Students’ Semantic Mistakes in Writing Seven Different Types of
SQL Queries.” <em>Proc. 2016 ACM Conference on Innovation and
Technology in Computer Science Education</em>, ahead of print, July. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2899415.2899464">10.1145/2899415.2899464</a>.
 <em>First large-scale analysis of SQL semantic errors by novices; 160k+ queries from 2300+ students over 9 years; majority of errors are omissions, especially in JOIN/subquery/GROUP BY; recommends explicitly teaching query-type selection.</em></p>
<p id="ahmed2016">
Ahmed, Tarek M., Cor-Paul Bezemer, Tse-Hsun Chen, Ahmed E. Hassan, and
Weiyi Shang. 2016. “Studying the Effectiveness of Application
Performance Management (APM) Tools for Detecting Performance Regressions
for Web Applications.” <em>Proc. 13th Conference on Mining
Software Repositories</em>, ahead of print, May. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2901739.2901774">10.1145/2901739.2901774</a>.
 <em>Studies performance regressions caused by software updates; contrasts research mining tools with industry APM tools for detecting performance issues via operational data.</em></p>
<p id="ahmed2021">
Ahmed, Zaheed, Eike Stein, Steffen Herbold, Fabian Trautsch, and Jens
Grabowski. 2021. “A New Perspective on the Competent Programmer
Hypothesis Through the Reproduction of Bugs with Repeated
Mutations.” <em>arXiv</em>, ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/ARXIV.2104.02517">10.48550/ARXIV.2104.02517</a>.
 <em>Tests the competent programmer hypothesis (bugs are near-correct code) by re-creating real bugs via mutation chains; hypothesis holds but mutation testing lacks operators to generate representative real-world bugs.</em></p>
<p id="aiken1975">
Aiken, Edwin G., Gary S. Thomas, and William A. Shennum. 1975.
“Memory for a Lecture: Effects of Notes, Lecture Rate, and
Informational Density.” <em>Journal of Educational
Psychology</em> 67 (June). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1037/h0076613">10.1037/h0076613</a>.
 <em>Study of 180 college students finds 48-hour lecture retention is best when note-taking is separated from listening and speech rate is normal or twice-through speeded.</em></p>
<p id="ait2022">
Ait, Adem, Javier Luis Cánovas Izquierdo, and Jordi Cabot. 2022.
“An Empirical Study on the Survival Rate of GitHub
Projects.” <em>Proc. 19th Conference on Mining Software
Repositories</em>, ahead of print, May. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3524842.3527941">10.1145/3524842.3527941</a>.
 <em>Longitudinal analysis of 1,127 GitHub repos from 4 ecosystems (NPM, R, WordPress, Laravel) created in 2016; development follows intensive coding bursts then long inactivity; survival probability falls below 50% after 5 years.</em></p>
<p id="aitchison2016">
Aitchison, Laurence, Nicola Corradi, and Peter E. Latham. 2016.
“Zipf’s Law Arises Naturally When There Are Underlying, Unobserved
Variables.” <em>PLOS Computational Biology</em> 12
(12). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005110">10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005110</a>.
 <em>Extends statistical-physics explanation of Zipf's law to a broader model class via simpler latent-variable mixing theory; applies to word frequencies, variable-length sequences, and multi-neuron spiking data; provides empirical verification methods.</em></p>
<p id="aivaloglou2021">
Aivaloglou, Efthimia, and Anna van der Meulen. 2021. “An Empirical
Study of Students’ Perceptions on the Setup and Grading of Group
Programming Assignments.” <em>ACM Transactions on Computing
Education</em> 21 (March). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3440994">10.1145/3440994</a>.
 <em>Interview study of 20 CS students from 4 universities on group programming assignment setup and grading; identifies team composition factors; finds three grading strategies with varied student perceptions; automated contribution metrics deemed not always representative.</em></p>
<p id="ajami2018">
Ajami, Shulamyt, Yonatan Woodbridge, and Dror G. Feitelson. 2018.
“Syntax, Predicates, Idioms—What Really Affects Code
Complexity?” <em>Empirical Software Engineering</em> 24 (1):
287–328. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s10664-018-9628-3">10.1007/s10664-018-9628-3</a>.
 <em>Game-like experiment with 220 professional programmers finds for loops harder than ifs, loops counting down harder than up, and comprehension time and error rate are not equivalent measures of difficulty.</em></p>
<p id="akerblom2015">
Åkerblom, Beatrice, and Tobias Wrigstad. 2015. “Measuring
Polymorphism in Python Programs.” <em>Proc. 11th
Symposium on Dynamic Languages</em>, ahead of print, October. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2816707.2816717">10.1145/2816707.2816717</a>.
 <em>Trace-based study of polymorphism in 36 OSS Python programs (7M+ call-sites); programs largely monomorphic; megamorphic call-sites rare but present; neither nominal nor structural typing can fully type entire programs.</em></p>
<p id="albert2020">
Albert, Jim, and Jingchen Hu. 2020. <em>Bayesian Computing in the
Undergraduate Statistics Curriculum</em>. February 22. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/arXiv.2002.09716">10.48550/arXiv.2002.09716</a>.
 <em>Overview of Bayesian computational methods for undergraduate stats education; compares approaches based on classroom experience; guides instructors on computation choice for specific learning outcomes.</em></p>
<p id="dahlbyalbright2018">
Albright, Sarah Dahlby, Titus H. Klinge, and Samuel A. Rebelsky. 2018.
“A Functional Approach to Data Science in CS1.” <em>Proc.
49th ACM Technical Symposium on Computer Science Education</em>, ahead
of print, February. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3159450.3159550">10.1145/3159450.3159550</a>.
 <em>Intro CS course blending data science (wrangling, visualization) with core CS concepts (recursion, linked structures) using Scheme/Racket; spiral 'use then implement' approach; includes data-for-social-good capstone.</em></p>
<p id="alesina2020">
Alesina, Alberto, Marlon Seror, David Yang, Yang You, and Weihong Zeng.
2020. <em>Persistence Despite Revolutions</em>. April. <a href="https://doi.org/10.3386/w27053">10.3386/w27053</a>.
 <em>Chinese Communist/Cultural Revolutions homogenized population economically short-term but grandchildren of pre-revolution elite still earn 16% more and have 11% more schooling today; elite values also transmitted intergenerationally, showing limits of social engineering.</em></p>
<p id="ali2020">
Ali, Rao Hamza, Chelsea Parlett-Pelleriti, and Erik Linstead. 2020.
“Cheating Death.” <em>Proc. 17th Conference on Mining
Software Repositories</em>, ahead of print, June. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3379597.3387511">10.1145/3379597.3387511</a>.
 <em>Survival analysis (Kaplan-Meier, Cox) of 3052 Python OSS projects over 165 months; multi-platform hosting, regular major releases, and larger developer networks predict project longevity.</em></p>
<p id="alkhabaz2021">
Alkhabaz, Ridha, Seth Poulsen, Mei Chen, and Abdussalam Alawini. 2021.
“Insights from Student Solutions to MongoDB Homework
Problems.” <em>Proc. International Conference on Software
Engineering (ICSE)</em>, June. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3430665.3456308">10.1145/3430665.3456308</a>.
 <em>Analysis of MongoDB homework errors from 527 students over 2 semesters; advanced operators cause more Reference errors; students improve after initial exposure to new operators; recommends more instructional time on advanced MongoDB concepts.</em></p>
<p id="allen2018">
Allen, Joseph A., Nale Lehmann-Willenbrock, and Steven G. Rogelberg.
2018. “Let’s Get This Meeting Started: Meeting Lateness and Actual
Meeting Outcomes.” <em>Journal of Organizational Behavior</em> 39
(March). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1002/job.2276">10.1002/job.2276</a>.
 <em>Three studies on meeting lateness: field study shows negative correlation with satisfaction/effectiveness; lab experiments confirm causal effect; group experiment shows impact on performance and socioemotional behavior.</em></p>
<p id="allen2025">
Allen, Stuart M., Neil Chue Hong, Stephan Druskat, et al. 2025. <em>Ten
Simple Rules for PIs to Integrate Research Software Engineering into
Their Research Group</em>. <a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.20217">https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.20217</a>.
 <em>Ten practical rules for PIs integrating Research Software Engineering into their groups; targets accessibility of RSEng practices to improve software quality, reproducibility, and trustworthiness.</em></p>
<p id="allman2012">
Allman, Eric. 2012. “Managing Technical Debt.”
<em>Communications of the ACM</em> 55 (May). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2160718.2160733">10.1145/2160718.2160733</a>.
 <em>Technical debt: shortcuts that reduce cost/time now impose larger future costs.</em></p>
<p id="almeida2017">
Almeida, Daniel A., Gail C. Murphy, Greg Wilson, and Mike Hoye. 2017.
“Do Software Developers Understand Open Source Licenses?”
<em>2017 25th Conference on Program Comprehension (ICPC)</em>, ahead of
print, May. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/icpc.2017.7">10.1109/icpc.2017.7</a>.
 <em>Survey of 375 developers on open source license comprehension (GPL3, LGPL3, MPL2); correct in 62% of 42 scenarios; single-license cases understood well but multi-license combinations are problematic; recommends tool support.</em></p>
<p id="dealmeida2022">
Almeida, Eduardo Santana de, Iftekhar Ahmed, and Andre van der Hoek.
2022. “Let’s Go to the Whiteboard (Again):perceptions from
Software Architects on Whiteboard Architecture Meetings.”
<em>arXiv</em>, ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/ARXIV.2210.16089">10.48550/ARXIV.2210.16089</a>.
 <em>Mixed-methods study of software architect whiteboard meetings; identifies 12 observations on technical/social aspects; covers motivations, documentation, post-meeting changes, and digital whiteboard use.</em></p>
<p id="alomar2022">
AlOmar, Eman Abdullah, Moataz Chouchen, Mohamed Wiem Mkaouer, and Ali
Ouni. 2022. <em>Code Review Practices for Refactoring Changes: An
Empirical Study on OpenStack</em>.
 <em>Study of 11,010 refactoring/non-refactoring code reviews in OpenStack; refactoring reviews take significantly longer; thematic analysis produces 28-criteria taxonomy of what developers evaluate when reviewing refactored code.</em></p>
<p id="alrimawi2022">
Alrimawi, Faeq, and Bashar Nuseibeh. 2022. “Kind
Computing.” <em>Proc. ACM/IEEE 44th Conference on Software
Engineering: New Ideas and Emerging Results</em>, ICSE ’22, May, 61–65.
<a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3510455.3512794">10.1145/3510455.3512794</a>.
 <em>Proposes kind computing paradigm: explicitly incorporating kindness into software development; identifies open SE research challenges and a research agenda; calls for new abstractions and tools.</em></p>
<p id="alsubaihin2021">
Al-Subaihin, Afnan A., Federica Sarro, Sue Black, Licia Capra, and Mark
Harman. 2021. “App Store Effects on Software Engineering
Practices.” <em>IEEE Transactions on Software
Engineering</em> 47 (2): 300–319. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2019.2891715">10.1109/tse.2019.2891715</a>.
 <em>Developer interviews and questionnaires on how app stores affect SE tasks; three themes: dev-user gap bridging, market transparency, mobile release management; implications for testing and requirements engineering.</em></p>
<p id="alsuhaibani2022">
Alsuhaibani, Reem S., Christian D. Newman, Michael J. Decker, Michael L.
Collard, and Jonathan I. Maletic. 2022. “An Approach to
Automatically Assess Method Names.” <em>Proceedings of the 30th
IEEE/ACM International Conference on Program
Comprehension</em>, May. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3524610.3527780">10.1145/3524610.3527780</a>.
 <em>Automated method naming quality assessment using 10 validated naming standards; employs NLP (POS tagging, identifier splitting, dictionary lookup); evaluated against expert ratings on manually constructed golden set.</em></p>
<p id="altadmri2015">
Altadmri, Amjad, and Neil C. C. Brown. 2015. “37 Million
Compilations.” <em>Proc. 46th ACM Technical Symposium on Computer
Science Education</em>, ahead of print, February. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2676723.2677258">10.1145/2676723.2677258</a>.
 <em>Analysis of compilation events from 250k+ students globally (Blackbox dataset); measures frequency, time-to-fix, and spread of programming errors; informs course and tool design to target frequent or hard-to-fix errors.</em></p>
<p id="alvidrez1999">
Alvidrez, Jennifer, and Rhona S. Weinstein. 1999. “Early Teacher
Perceptions and Later Student Academic Achievement.” <em>Journal
of Educational Psychology</em> 91 (December). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-0663.91.4.731">10.1037/0022-0663.91.4.731</a>.
 <em>Preschool teachers over/underestimates of IQ (N=110) significantly predict GPA and SAT-taking 14 years later; effect strongest for underestimated children; SES and perceived maturity drive biased teacher judgments.</em></p>
<p id="ameller2012">
Ameller, David, Claudia Ayala, Jordi Cabot, and Xavier Franch. 2012.
“How Do Software Architects Consider Non-Functional Requirements:
An Exploratory Study.” <em>Proc. International Requirements
Engineering Conference (RE)</em>, September. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/re.2012.6345838">10.1109/re.2012.6345838</a>.
 <em>Interview study of 13 software architects on NFR practices; identifies who decides NFRs, which types matter most, and how they are documented and validated; contextualizes findings with prior work.</em></p>
<p id="ames2018">
Ames, Morgan G. 2018. “Hackers, Computers, and Cooperation: A
Critical History of Logo and Constructionist Learning.” <em>Proc.
ACM on Human-Computer Interaction</em> 2 (November). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3274287">10.1145/3274287</a>.
 <em>Historical analysis of constructionism/Logo traces individualistic, anti-authority assumptions into current CSCW/CSCL technologies (Scratch, FabLabs); critiques atomized view of collaboration rooted in hacker culture.</em></p>
<p id="amir2026">
Amir, Dorsa, Richard E. Ahl, Matthew R. Jordan, et al. 2026. “The
Emergence of Cooperative Behaviors, Norms, and Strategies Across Five
Diverse Societies.” <em>Science Advances</em> 12 (6). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1126/sciadv.adw9995">10.1126/sciadv.adw9995</a>.
 <em>Cross-cultural study of 413 children aged 5-13 from five societies finds substantial variation in cooperative behaviors, but convergence toward community-specific norms in middle childhood.</em></p>
<p id="amit2021">
Amit, Idan, Nili Ben Ezra, and Dror G. Feitelson. 2021. “Follow
Your Nose - Which Code Smells Are Worth Chasing?” <em>arXiv</em>,
ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/ARXIV.2103.01861">10.48550/ARXIV.2103.01861</a>.
 <em>Empirical analysis of 151 code smells in 31k+ Java files from 677 repos; &lt;20% are potentially causal for quality/productivity; strongest smells involve simplicity and defensive programming; files without causal smells 50% more likely high quality; developers rarely remove effective smells.</em></p>
<p id="amjad2024">
Amjad, Abdul Haddi, Muhammad Danish, Bless Jah, and Muhammad Ali Gulzar.
2024. <em>Accessibility Issues in Ad-Driven Web Applications</em>.
September 27. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/arXiv.2409.18590">10.48550/arXiv.2409.18590</a>.
 <em>Large-scale study of 430K web elements including 100K ads; 67% of websites have increased WCAG violations from third-party ads; 27% of WCAG-compliant ads have misleading alt text; screen reader users forced to expose data via hover events to navigate ads.</em></p>
<p id="anaraki2024">
Anaraki, Nazanin Tabatabaei, Taneisha Ng, Gaurav Verma, et al. 2024.
“Managing Project Teams in an Online Class of 1000+
Students.” <em>arXiv</em>, ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/ARXIV.2412.11046">10.48550/ARXIV.2412.11046</a>.
 <em>10-year experience managing 200+ project teams with 1000+ globally distributed grad students in an online CS course; describes team formation, iterative feedback, and peer interaction strategies for large-scale online SE education.</em></p>
<p id="anda2009">
Anda, B. C. D., D. I. K. Sjoberg, and A. Mockus. 2009.
“Variability and Reproducibility in Software Engineering: A Study
of Four Companies That Developed the Same System.” <em>IEEE
Transactions on Software Engineering</em> 35 (May). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2008.89">10.1109/tse.2008.89</a>.
 <em>Longitudinal multiple-case study: 4 companies built same system from same spec; price/schedule had low reproducibility, usability high, reliability/maintainability low; reproducibility remains a major unsolved challenge in SE.</em></p>
<p id="anderson2015">
Anderson, Eric, Song Lin, Duncan Simester, and Catherine Tucker. 2015.
“Harbingers of Failure.” <em>Journal of Marketing
Research</em> 52 (October). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1509/jmr.13.0415">10.1509/jmr.13.0415</a>.
 <em>Identifies harbingers of failure: customers who systematically purchase new products that flop; their early adoption predicts product failure; challenges assumption that positive customer feedback signals future success.</em></p>
<p id="anderson2025">
Anderson, Felicity, Julien Sindt, and Neil Chue Hong. 2025. <em>Who Do
You Think You Are? Creating RSE Personas from GitHub Interactions</em>.
<a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.05390">https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.05390</a>.
 <em>Data-driven RSE personas from mining 115K contributors across 1,284 GitHub repos; identifies 7 personas (Ephemeral to Active Contributor); demonstrates scalable characterization despite project heterogeneity.</em></p>
<p id="anderson2007">
Anderson, Melissa S., Emily A. Ronning, Raymond De Vries, and Brian C.
Martinson. 2007. “The Perverse Effects of Competition on
Scientists’ Work and Relationships.” <em>Science and Engineering
Ethics</em> 13 (November). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s11948-007-9042-5">10.1007/s11948-007-9042-5</a>.
 <em>Focus groups with 51 scientists reveal that pervasive competition contributes to strategic game-playing, reduced information sharing, interference with peer review, and careless research conduct.</em></p>
<p id="aniche2021a">
Aniche, Mauricio, Frank Mulder, and Felienne Hermans. 2021.
“Grading 600+ Students: A Case Study on Peer and Self
Grading.” <em>2021 43rd Conference on Software Engineering:
Software Engineering Education and Training (ICSE-SEET)</em>, May,
211–20. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/icse-seet52601.2021.00031">10.1109/icse-seet52601.2021.00031</a>.
 <em>Self/peer grading study in SE course (906 submissions); self grades run 8-10% higher than peer grades; peer grades approximate TA grades; gender and nationality do not affect grading behavior.</em></p>
<p id="aniche2021b">
Aniche, Mauricio, Christoph Treude, and Andy Zaidman. 2021. “How
Developers Engineer Test Cases: An Observational Study.” <em>IEEE
Transactions on Software Engineering</em>, ahead of print. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2021.3129889">10.1109/tse.2021.3129889</a>.
 <em>Using think-aloud observations of 13 developers and a survey of 72 more, this study examines how developers reason about and approach manual test case design, proposing a framework and three core testing strategies to guide future research and practice.</em></p>
<p id="anvik2006">
Anvik, John, Lyndon Hiew, and Gail C. Murphy. 2006. “Who Should
Fix This Bug?” <em>Proceedings of the 28th International
Conference on Software Engineering</em>, ICSE06, May, 361–70. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/1134285.1134336">10.1145/1134285.1134336</a>.
 <em>ML-based semi-automated bug report triage assigns reports to developers; 57-64% precision on Eclipse/Firefox; lower success on gcc; describes conditions for applicability and lessons from mining open bug repositories.</em></p>
<p id="apel2011">
Apel, Sven, Jörg Liebig, Benjamin Brandl, Christian Lengauer, and
Christian Kästner. 2011. “Semistructured Merge: Rethinking Merge
in Revision Control Systems.” <em>Proc. European Software
Engineering Conference/International Symposium on the Foundations of
Software Engineering (ESEC/FSE)</em>. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2025113.2025141">10.1145/2025113.2025141</a>.
 <em>Semistructured merge combines generality of text-based and expressiveness of language-specific revision control via annotated grammars; study on 24 projects shows 34% conflict reduction in 60% of scenarios; renaming increases conflicts.</em></p>
<p id="junior2009">
Aquino Junior, Gibeon Soares de, and Silvio Romero de Lemos Meira. 2009.
“Towards Effective Productivity Measurement in Software
Projects.” <em>2009 Fourth Conference on Software Engineering
Advances</em>, ahead of print, September. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/icsea.2009.44">10.1109/icsea.2009.44</a>.
 <em>Reviews productivity measurement in software organizations; proposes a Value Size Metrics framework and a process for defining organization-specific productivity models aligned with management goals.</em></p>
<p id="aranda2023">

 <em>12 quasi-experiments (N=124) on experience vs. requirements elicitation effectiveness; in unfamiliar domains experience has no effect; in familiar domains interview experience helps but professional experience slightly hurts.</em></p>

 <em>Ethics integration across a stats/data science undergrad major via top-to-bottom curriculum and co-curricular programming; describes 6 portable ethics modules across 5 courses; reports effectiveness assessment.</em></p>

<p id="bayman1983">

<p id="becker2018a">

<p id="begel2014">

<p id="behroozi2020b">

<p id="beller2019">

Proksch, Sven Amann, and Andy Zaidman. 2019. “Developer Testing in

 <em>Large-scale field study of 2,443 SE engineers over 2.5 years in 4 IDEs; half do not test; TDD not widely practiced; 12% of tests flaky; actual test time is 25% vs. perceived 50%; introduces Test-Guided Development (TGD).</em></p>
<p id="beller2015b">

<p id="beller2018">

<p id="beller2015a">

<p id="bernstein2018a">

<p id="blelloch1989">

<p id="blesch2022">

<p id="bloom1984">

<p id="bluedorn1999">

 <em>Dataset and materials from a controlled experiment (105 participants) on REST API design rule adherence vs. understandability; includes raw data, cleaning protocol, R analysis script, and OpenAPI documents.</em></p>
<p id="bogner2022">
Bogner, Justus, and Manuel Merkel. 2022. “To Type or Not to

 <em>Mining study of 604 GitHub projects (JS vs TS); TS has significantly better code quality and understandability; contrary to expectations, TS bug proneness and resolution time are not better than JS.</em></p>
<p id="bogomolov2021">
Bogomolov, Egor, Vladimir Kovalenko, Yurii Rebryk, Alberto Bacchelli,

 <em>Language-agnostic source code authorship attribution approach; accuracy on synthetic datasets drops significantly on realistic data; argues existing datasets poorly reflect practical SE use cases.</em></p>
<p id="bohay2011">

<p id="borg2022">

<p id="borg2024">

Notations, Tools, and Environments</em>, ahead of print, October. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3623504.3623567">10.1145/3623504.3623567</a>.
 <em>jq's pure-functional concatenative evaluation model confuses users; visualization of recursively forking execution on actual data with live editing affordances clarifies behavior and aids filter construction.</em></p>
<p id="hora2021a">
Hora, Andre. 2021a. “Googling for Software Development: What
Developers Search for and What They Find.” <em>2021 18th

 <em>Analysis of 1.3M web queries to programming sites: queries are short (3 words), keyword-first, omit function words; Stack Overflow dominates results; minor query changes have small but non-negligible impact.</em></p>
<p id="hora2021b">
Hora, Andre. 2021b. “What Code Is Deliberately Excluded from Test

 <em>First study of coverage exclusion in 55 Python projects: 1/3 exclude code; developers exclude non-runnable, debug, defensive, and platform-specific code; most excluded code was already untested or complex.</em></p>
<p id="horn2023">

<p id="horton2023">

of print, March. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3017680.3017724">10.1145/3017680.3017724</a>.
 <em>Multi-year study shows high school students model variable assignment as lazy evaluation of stored expressions; x = x + 1 is seen as impossible, rooted in algebraic equality intuition.</em></p>

<p id="kolikant2008">

 <em>Historical perspective on how RISC architectures, C, and Unix co-evolved through industry dynamics and contingent events to reshape computing from the 1980s through the RISC golden age (1986-1996).</em></p>
<p id="mason2016">

 <em>CLT-driven redesign of a database course removes split-attention and redundancy effects; exam failure rate dropped 34% for mid-to-lower performers on identical exams after the redesign.</em></p>
<p id="masood2020">

<p id="mathews2024">

<p id="metcalfe2017">

<p id="meyer2021">

<p id="miller2022a">
Miller, Courtney, Sophie Cohen, Daniel Klug, Bogdan Vasilescu, and
Christian KaUstner. 2022. “"Did You Miss My Comment or What?":
Understanding Toxicity in Open Source Discussions.”
<em>Proceedings of the 44th International Conference on Software
Engineering</em>, ICSE ’22, May, 710–22. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/3510003.3510111">10.1145/3510003.3510111</a>.
 <em>Qualitative analysis of 100 toxic GitHub issue discussions; prevalent forms: entitled/demanding users and insults from technical disagreements; project members also authors of toxicity; different patterns from Reddit/Wikipedia toxicity.</em></p>
<p id="miller2014">
Miller, Craig S. 2014. “Metonymy and Reference-Point Errors in
Novice Programming.” <em>Computer Science Education</em> 24
(July). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1080/08993408.2014.952500">10.1080/08993408.2014.952500</a>.
 <em>Student reference-point errors in programming follow metonymic patterns; identifying attributes are referenced more than descriptive ones, suggesting students rely on communicative habits rather than mechanistic reasoning.</em></p>
<p id="miller2016">
Miller, Craig S., and Amber Settle. 2016. “Some Trouble with
Transparency.” <em>Proc. 2016 ACM Conference on International
Computing Education Research</em>, ahead of print, August. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1145/2960310.2960327">10.1145/2960310.2960327</a>.
 <em>Most intro Python OOP students omit self or fail to use it to access attributes; reference errors dominate over indentation or return errors, linked to difficulties with parameter passing and dot notation.</em></p>
<p id="miller2015">
Miller, David I., and Jonathan Wai. 2015. “The Bachelor’s to Ph.d.
STEM Pipeline No Longer Leaks More Women Than Men: A 30-Year
Analysis.” <em>Frontiers in Psychology</em> 6 (February). <a href="https://doi.org/10.3389/fpsyg.2015.00037">10.3389/fpsyg.2015.00037</a>.
 <em>Retrospective longitudinal analysis shows the STEM leaky pipeline closed for bachelor's-to-PhD women in the 1990s; current underrepresentation must be understood at and below the bachelor's level.</em></p>
<p id="miller1956">
Miller, George A. 1956. “The Magical Number Seven, Plus or Minus
Two: Some Limits on Our Capacity for Processing Information.”
<em>Psychological Review</em> 63 (2): 81–97. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1037/h0043158">10.1037/h0043158</a>.
 <em>Working memory is limited to ~7 chunks; chunking and recoding expand effective capacity; information theory provides a quantitative framework for studying attention, memory, and learning.</em></p>
<p id="miller2013">
Miller, Kelly, Nathaniel Lasry, Kelvin Chu, and Eric Mazur. 2013.
“Role of Physics Lecture Demonstrations in Conceptual
Learning.” <em>Physical Review Special Topics - Physics Education
Research</em> 9 (September). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1103/physrevstper.9.020113">10.1103/physrevstper.9.020113</a>.
 <em>~1-in-5 lecture demonstration observations are inconsistent with actual outcomes; having prior knowledge or predicting before observing each independently raise correct observation rates by ~20%.</em></p>
<p id="miller2011">
Miller, Michelle D. 2011. “What College Teachers Should Know about
Memory: A Perspective from Cognitive Psychology.” <em>College
Teaching</em> 59 (July). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1080/87567555.2011.580636">10.1080/87567555.2011.580636</a>.
 <em>Overview of short-term, working, and long-term memory theories for instructors; emphasizes memory as an adaptive system shaped by natural selection and recommends frequent testing to exploit how it works.</em></p>
<p id="miltner2018">
Miltner, Kate M. 2018. “Girls Who Coded: Gender in Twentieth
Century u.k. And u.s. Computing.” <em>Science, Technology, &amp;
Human Values</em> 44 (May). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1177/0162243918770287">10.1177/0162243918770287</a>.
 <em>Reviews the Facebook code review gender dispute and broader literature to argue that gender and technology are co-constitutive; teaching girls to code cannot undo structural power dynamics built into systems over decades.</em></p>
<p id="minahan1986">
Minahan, Anne. 1986. “"Martha’s Rules": An Alternative to Robert’s
Rules of Order.” <em>Affilia</em> 1 (2): 53–56. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1177/088610998600100206">10.1177/088610998600100206</a>.
 <em>Martha's Rules provide a structured consensus decision-making alternative to Robert's Rules, enabling feminist and cooperative organizations to make decisions efficiently while preserving participatory values.</em></p>
<p id="mirhosseini2020">
Mirhosseini, Samim, and Chris Parnin. 2020. “Docable: Evaluating
the Executability of Software Tutorials.” <em>Proc. 28th ACM
Joint Meeting on European Software Engineering Conference and Symposium

 <em>Empirical study of 600+ tutorials and 15,000 code blocks finds only 26% execute successfully even with human annotation; missing steps, inaccessible resources, and interactive prompts are the main barriers.</em></p>
<p id="mirzamomen2023">
Mirzamomen, Zahra, and Marcel Böhme. 2023. <em>Finding Bug-Inducing
Program Environments</em>. April 20. <a href="https://doi.org/10.48550/arXiv.2304.10044">10.48550/arXiv.2304.10044</a>.
 <em>AFLChaos intercepts and mutates system calls to generate coverage-guided bug-inducing environments; found bugs in 5 of 7 projects including OpenSSL without any environment modeling.</em></p>
<p id="mitchell2010">
Mitchell, N., E. Schonberg, and G. Sevitsky. 2010. “Four Trends
Leading to Java Runtime Bloat.” <em>IEEE Software</em> 27 (1):
56–63. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/ms.2010.7">10.1109/ms.2010.7</a>.
 <em>Argues that abstraction, OOP, and reusable libraries have improved productivity but large Java applications show that productivity improvements do not always outweigh performance costs.</em></p>
<p id="mitropoulos2019">
Mitropoulos, Dimitris, Panos Louridas, Vitalis Salis, and Diomidis
Spinellis. 2019. “Time Present and Time Past: Analyzing the

 <em>9-month daily snapshots of JavaScript from Alexa top-10K sites show scripts change every few days; quality issues persist over time; vulnerable third-party libraries decrease while code reuse remains widespread.</em></p>
<p id="miyatsu2018">
Miyatsu, Toshiya, Khuyen Nguyen, and Mark A. McDaniel. 2018. “Five

<p id="mladenovic2017">

<p id="mo2021">
Mo, Ran, Yuanfang Cai, Rick Kazman, Lu Xiao, and Qiong Feng. 2021.
“Architecture Anti-Patterns: Automatically Detectable Violations

 <em>Analysis of 19 large-scale software projects shows architecture anti-patterns significantly increase bug-proneness and change-proneness, with Unstable Interface and Crossing contributing most.</em></p>
<p id="mockus2010">
Mockus, Audris. 2010. “Organizational Volatility and Its Effects
on Software Defects.” <em>Proc. Eighteenth ACM SIGSOFT

 <em>Developer-centric organizational change metrics correlate with customer-reported defects; proximity to org change reduces quality; recent departures increase defect probability; distributed development decreases quality.</em></p>
<p id="mockus2000">

<p id="moe2010">

<p id="mohayeji2025">

<p id="mokhov2020">

<p id="molder2021">

<p id="moldon2021">

<p id="monnier2020">

<p id="moore2025">

<p id="lopez2018">

<p id="morehead2019b">

<p id="morehead2019a">

<p id="morrison2016">

 <em>Subgoal-labeled instruction for while loops assessed via Parsons problems shows given labels outperform both no-label and self-generated-label conditions; Parsons problems detect learning gains more sensitively than code generation.</em></p>
<p id="mueller2014">

(April). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1177/0956797614524581">10.1177/0956797614524581</a>.
 <em>Three studies show laptop note-takers transcribe verbatim and perform worse on conceptual questions; longhand forces reframing which produces deeper processing and better learning outcomes.</em></p>
<p id="muhammad2019">

<p id="mukherjee2023">

<p id="muller2015">

<p id="munaiah2017">

<p id="murphy2008">

<p id="nagappan2015">

<p id="nagappan2008a">

<p id="nagappan2008b">

<p id="nakajo1991">

 <em>Study of 1.4M GitHub Jupyter notebooks finds most are not reproducible due to out-of-order execution and missing dependencies; proposes best practices for improving notebook reproducibility.</em></p>
<p id="pinckney2022">

 <em>PacSolve/MaxNPM replaces NPM's greedy dependency solver with customizable constraint optimization; reduces vulnerabilities in 33% of cases, selects newer/fewer dependencies; evaluated on large NPM samples.</em></p>
<p id="pinto2022">

 <em>Case study of Cognitive Driven Development (CDD) at a Brazilian company; limiting code unit complexity via CDD keeps units small and makes testing easier, though developers relax limits under pressure.</em></p>

<p id="robatishirzad2024">

 <em>Ruxanne tool mines top 18 Rust GitHub projects to identify 20 bug fix pattern groups; most common general pattern is adding/removing struct fields and most common borrow-checker pattern is removing clone() calls.</em></p>

<p id="rohrer2015">

<p id="rombaut2023">

<p id="rosa2024">

(VL/HCC)</em>, October, 233–37. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/vlhcc.2017.8103472">10.1109/vlhcc.2017.8103472</a>.
 <em>Replication of 2001/2003 salary analyses using 2012 data; workers using spreadsheets and doing programming earn ~10% more than similar workers who do neither, controlling for employment and demographics.</em></p>
<p id="scalabrino2021">
Scalabrino, Simone, Gabriele Bavota, Christopher Vendome, Mario
Linares-Vásquez, Denys Poshyvanyk, and Rocco Oliveto. 2021.

Transactions on Software Engineering</em> 47 (March). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2019.2901468">10.1109/tse.2019.2901468</a>.
 <em>Evaluation of 121 metrics (code, documentation, developer) for predicting understandability using 444 human ratings; no single metric captures understandability; even combined models are insufficient for practical use.</em></p>
<p id="scalabrino2018">
Scalabrino, Simone, Mario Linares-Vásquez, Rocco Oliveto, and Denys
Poshyvanyk. 2018. “A Comprehensive Model for Code
Readability.” <em>Journal of Software: Evolution and Process</em>
30 (June). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1002/smr.1958">10.1002/smr.1958</a>.
 <em>Textual features improve code readability prediction; combined model (structural + textual) significantly outperforms state-of-the-art on 600+ snippets rated by 5k+ people; better readability predicts FindBugs warnings.</em></p>
<p id="scanlan1989">

 <em>Experiment showing structured flowcharts produce faster, more accurate algorithm comprehension than pseudocode for conditional logic; advantage holds across algorithms of varying complexity.</em></p>
<p id="scanniello2017">

 <em>Family of 4 experiments (100 participants) finds no difference in fault-fixing effort, effectiveness, or efficiency between abbreviated and full-word identifier names; abbreviated names prompt more methodical review behavior.</em></p>
<p id="scarsbrook2023">

<p id="schantong2024">

<p id="shome2022">

 <em>Introduces catalog of 14 data smells (analogous to code smells) indicating quality issues in ML datasets; identified by analyzing 25 public datasets; provides early-warning indicators for ML technical debt.</em></p>
<p id="shore2010">

<p id="shreeve2022">

(May). <a href="https://doi.org/10.1109/tse.2020.3023735">10.1109/tse.2020.3023735</a>.
 <em>Tabletop game study of 208 sessions (948 players) finds no group of security experts makes better decisions than others; diverse teams and homogeneous expert teams perform similarly; expertise biases lead to blind spots.</em></p>
<p id="shrestha2018">

<p id="shrestha2021b">

<p id="shtulman2017">

<p id="shumskithomas2017">

<p id="silva2016">

<p id="silva2017">

<p id="silva2020a">

<p id="silva2020b">

<p id="silva2022">

<p id="simon2013">

<p id="simon2021">

<p id="siochi2015">

<p id="smarr2018">

<p id="smirnov2023">

<p id="soloway1984">

<p id="soltani2020">

<p id="sondergaard2012">

<p id="soremekun2021">

 <em>Comparison of statistical fault localization vs. dynamic slicing on 457 bugs in 46 C programs; dynamic slicing is 8% more effective for single faults; hybrid approach (top-5 statistical then slicing) examines only 15% of code on average.</em></p>
<p id="sorva2008">

<p id="sorva2013b">

 <em>ProgTest integrates programming and testing in CS intro courses via automated web-based evaluation; preliminary results show improved student understanding and performance.</em></p>

<p id="spinellis2016">

 <em>RICK tool automatically generates Java unit tests with realistic mocks and stubs by observing executing applications; monitors method invocations and external interactions; produces mock-based oracles from runtime data.</em></p>
<p id="tiwari2024">

 <em>Case studies of humor in three OSS projects (faker, lolcommits, volkswagen) and survey of 125 developers; humor increases engagement and helps with hard engineering tasks; tests and documentation are the best places to practice humor responsibly.</em></p>
<p id="to2020">

<p id="trang2021">
Trang, Simon, and Welf H. Weiger. 2021. “The Perils of

<p id="trautsch2023">

 <em>Classifies 125k commits as quality-improving using a DL model fine-tuned on 2,533 manually-labeled commits; perfective changes improve static metrics; corrective changes add complexity; quality-improving commits are smaller than others.</em></p>
<p id="traver2010">

<p id="tregubov2017">

<p id="treude2023">

 <em>First analysis of testing technical debt in 177 R packages; common smells are inadequate/obscure tests and improper asserts; survey of R developers shows time constraints and poor tool documentation hinder testing quality.</em></p>
<p id="vidoni2022">

<p id="walter2018">

<p id="widyasari2023">

 <em>DECA algorithm (inspired by coevolution theory) identifies informatively easy and hard programming concepts; applied to problet tutor data; results inform instructors on which concepts to emphasize and contribute to CS concept inventories.</em></p>
<p id="wiese2014">

 <em>Finds that including fraction symbols alongside diagrams decreases performance by triggering whole-number transfer and revealing students lack the qualitative reasoning the diagrams are intended to develop.</em></p>
<p id="wiese2021">

 <em>Study of 125 undergraduates on Boolean short-circuit evaluation; students frequently omit edge-case checks or separate them in their own if-statements; only 35% recognize ordering errors in conjoined conditions vs. 54% in nested ifs.</em></p>
